< Text>
I found them via Google. I liked the reviews & the photos seemed nice. I called & was able to get a sameday appointment on a Saturday. So at the sceduled time, drove across town to drop our dog off for grooming. Upon arrival I was asked for the dogs shot records, which I did not think to bring with me.

We usually take our dog to another groomer but being that they were booked far in advance, I was just wanting to get our dog groomed since he was past due.

So here I was standing with dog in hand, being refused service because I didn't bring the paperwork with me. It is not a habit to take the dog's medical records with me every time I go out.

Their facility isn't as appears in the Google search results. Actually looks like they've down-sized & the dogs are in little random fenced areas.

Being a business who does this every day, they should make it a standard practice to notify new customers of what to bring with on the first visit.

So hence the 2-star rating. People don't need to be misled or misinformed, especially when it wastes their time/weekend.< /Text>

< text>
Won Ton Soup - Broth was very bland and not flavorful.  Wontons were better, good balance of wonton wrapper and filling, and the filling was moderately tasty and not gristly at all, great consistency.  Other ingredients (bok choi and carrots) were fresh and cooked well.  Overall, 3/5 stars for this dish

Beef Chow Fun - Good amount of beef and it was tender, but a little bland.  Noodles were well covered in sauce and not all stuck together with white parts inside.  Sauce was on the bland side.  Adding soy helped a lot.  3/5 stars

Mongolian Beef - Generous portion.  Very, very salty; it ended up mixing well with the chow fun (rice would have probably worked too) but I think I would have had a hard time eating it straight.  Nice heat kick at the end.  2/5 stars.

Service was friendly, 4/5 stars< /text>

< text>
Had an amazing evening during the Fringe Festival here!  I have walked by this building many times, but never had a reason to go in.  It's very old inside, but in that charming kind of way.  There seems to be multiple venues of varying size inside the building.  The only downside while we were here is that the elevator was broken, and the performance we were going to was on the top (4th or 5th?) floor.  The staircases seemed endless.  There was a really neat rooftop stage, where I imagine they hold some pretty neat performances.

The stage that we went to had about 50 chairs inside, with the stage set up front.  The sound and lighting was good, and the performance was amazing (Around the World in 80 Years).

Overall, this seems like an awesome venue.  I look forward to seeing more performances here!< /text>

<UserId.>106440082770575094057</UserId.>< text>
My wedding was over nine months ago, and I feel we're in a good place to finally leave a review. We are not naive; we understand that the photos and videos Joey shares on his website and social media are a small margin compared to the entirety of the events he shoots. Our venue recommended him, and he's got an impressive studio. We were sold. A few things to look out for: When signing the contract - the prices are all tied to prints at the end, not the actual event. Please please keep an eye on this, as you will spend thousands of dollars on prints that should cost a fraction of that. Not only did we pick the top plan because we wanted to work with Joey, but we also added on the photo booth. This was $5000-6000 in total. Joey was fun to work with on the day of the wedding; I cannot stress that enough. He's a good guy and a good photographer. With that being said, the entirety of the process left a lot to be desired. A month or so after the wedding we received a link of a batch of photos that were edited, and we were pleasantly surprised. Nothing that was a once-in-a-lifetime shot, but good pictures. We were so excited to see more. And then, a link went out to our entire family with 1200 unedited photos. Weird faces, bad angles, overexposure, and they were all for sale. Every picture was a sale opportunity. We then received calls from everyone - "why is this photo of me online; it's horrible!" They were bad photos of our parent, me (groom), and my wife (bride). It was a terrible look and left a bad taste in everyone's mouth. More importantly, that link he originally sent was it; those were the good photos we were getting. We ended up with dozens of overexposed photos, blurry photos, and grainy photos from the night shots. The same shots he's done at the same venue hundreds of times. They point blank weren't great, and absolutely not for what we spent on them. We left our wedding day with about 12 photos we really love. His excuse was the sun, our light sensitivity, etc. It would have been better just to say, "it wasn't my best day." After all of this, your left with the massive credit I discussed earlier. Oh, and you don't get ANY photos unless you spend the entire credit on his 500% marked up prices. So we did that. $28 for every little 5x7 photo. $34 for the 8x10 images. These are $5-10 on most sites like Mpix for the highest of quality. We wanted to order a book for our in-laws - it was nearly $1500. It has 30 photos in it, it's called The Redwood Album, and it can be recreated for around $300 on almost every single photography print website on the planet. Period. I left another review on this page the day after our wedding, and it was glowing - he was fun to work with. But wow, everything else was a real nightmare. Be sure to ask a ton of questions up front about pricing, because there is some dangerous smoke and mirrors happening on that front. Also, don't allow a professional photographer who shoots weddings to complain about the sun's placement during a 5:30 pm wedding. I believe Joey Ikemoto is a good person and a good photographer. I also think he really dropped the ball on our wedding and was paid handsomely to do that. Our wedding was 6/2/18, and we received our final photos on 3/28/19. This was because we hadn't used up our credit for him to mark up the images and collect on. We finally just ordered anything to move on. Luckily, we're in love and remember a fantastic day, even if there were only overexposed photos of our ceremony, and not a single picture of the dance routine we spent months preparing for - no sunlight in there to blame.<//text>

< review>
We got married at the Wayfarer's Chapel in October.  We looked at several photographer options.  We only needed a photographer  for the ceremony since we were from out of town and our reception would be later at a different venue.  We are also not a typical couple,  both of us being over 6'3 and I have a medical condition  that I am insecure about especially in pictures.  We also wanted photographer's who knew how to work with the Wayfarer's chapel, which is all glass so has specific lighting issues, and a short alotted time to get married which is very regimented and limited so we knew we had to make the time count and wanted the best we could get.
There were so many reasons we chose Joey and his colleagues.  First they were very flexible with what we needed, they had a package that met our needs where other photographers did not (we didn't need an engagement session and only needed hours at the church, and no reception coverage).   They are very affordable, especially for their high quality services, and offer many different packages.  They  have photographed weddings at the Wayfarer's church for years so they were so familiar with the best spots to get the best shots, especially at 2:00 in the afternoon (the hardest light time in the day), and they knew how to move us around the church to get the great shots while being discrete so guests and we didn't see each other before the ceremony. The church staff the whole time also said how they love when Joey & his team photograph, and they really worked well with each other to coordinate our time.   They were familiar with the lighting issues and structure of the church knowing where to stand and be to get the best coverage of our event.   They are also all very educated in their field, and receive a lot of training, and from what I can tell are  required to do continued education and trainings to stay expert in their skills.
Our photographer was Henry and his assistant.  We met with Joey a couple days before.  I asked if they could work around my condition, and went over how things would flow and what was important to us.
On the day of our wedding, Henry was there before us to meet.  Without even a flinch or a whole new discussion, he simply affirmed he went over everything with Joey, and understood what we needed, and gave me a nod and assured me what I had talked with Joey about and I had nothing to worry about.  This in itself was worth everything to me!  Everything! It can be so hard to have to go over things again and again, and see how people react ect, and right off he never had a reaction and made me feel at ease. He was so kind, so professional, organized, and really knew how to work in a very fast and effective way to make everyone feel comfortable,  get what he needed from everyone, even the kids,  and maximized the limited time we had to get all the important pictures we needed.
I would recommend Joey and his colleagues over and over without any hesitation.  Especially if you are getting married at the Wayfarer's Chapel.
We were so blessed to have had a dream wedding at a dream venue and the best photographers to capture it all!
On your special day,  you only get one chance to get things right!  One chance to capture it the way you hope it can be, and want the best you can get who can get it right, which without a doubt they did!<//review>
